     <p><b>Queen's University at Kingston</b><sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roycha_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roycha-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theo_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theo-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> (commonly shortened to <b>Queen's University</b> or <b>Queen's</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston</a>, Ontario, Canada. Founded on 16 October 1841, the university predated the founding of Canada by 26 years.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's holds more than 1,400 hectares (3,500 acres) of land throughout Ontario and owns <a href="/wiki/Herstmonceux_Castle" title="Herstmonceux Castle">Herstmonceux Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/East_Sussex" title="East Sussex">East Sussex</a>, England.<sup id="cite_ref-land_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-land-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's is organized into ten undergraduate, graduate and professional faculties and schools.<sup id="cite_ref-ugpfs_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ugpfs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> established Queen's College in 1841 with a royal charter from <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>. The first classes, intended to prepare students for the ministry, were held 7 March 1842 with 13 students and two professors.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's was the first university west of the maritime provinces to admit women, and to form a student government. In 1883, a women's college for medical education affiliated with Queen's University. In 1888, Queen's University began offering extension courses, becoming the first Canadian university to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1912, Queen's secularized and changed to its present legal name.</p> 
     <p>Queen's is a co-educational university, with more than 23,000 students, and with over 131,000 living alumni worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-Quick_Facts_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quick_Facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable alumni include government officials, academics, business leaders and 56 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhode_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhode-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The university ranked 175th in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-QS_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> 201-225th in the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> and 201-300 in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>. Queen's varsity teams, known as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gaels" title="Queen's Gaels" class="mw-redirect">Golden Gaels</a>, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>.</p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc">

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kingstonhall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Theological Hall at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kingstonhall.JPG/230px-Kingstonhall.JPG" width="230" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kingstonhall.JPG/345px-Kingstonhall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kingstonhall.JPG/460px-Kingstonhall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kingstonhall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Theological Hall originally served as Queen's University's main building throughout the late 19th century
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's was a result of an outgrowth of educational initiatives planned by Presbyterians in the 1830s. A draft plan for the university was presented at a <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">synod</a> meeting in Kingston in 1839, with a modified bill introduced through the <a href="/wiki/13th_Parliament_of_Upper_Canada" title="13th Parliament of Upper Canada">13th Parliament of Upper Canada</a> during a session in 1840.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> In 16 October 1841, a royal charter was issued through <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>. Queen's resulted from years of effort by Presbyterians of <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a> to found a college for the education of ministers in the growing colony and to instruct the youth in various branches of science and literature. They modelled the university after the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Classes began on 7 March 1842, in a small wood-frame house on the edge of the city with two professors and 15 students.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The college moved several times during its first eleven years, before settling in its present location.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>, the college was financially supported by the Presbyterian Church in Scotland, the Canadian government and private citizens. After Confederation the college faced ruin when the federal government withdrew its funding and the Commercial Bank of the Midland District collapsed, a disaster which cost Queen's two-thirds of its <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment#College_and_university_endowments" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a>. The college was rescued after Principal <a href="/wiki/William_Snodgrass_(clergyman)" title="William Snodgrass (clergyman)">William Snodgrass</a> and other officials created a fundraising campaign across Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The risk of financial ruin continued to worry the administration until the final decade of the century. They actively considered leaving Kingston and merging with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> as late as the 1880s.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> With the additional funds bequeathed from Queen's first major benefactor, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Sutherland" title="Robert Sutherland">Robert Sutherland</a>, the college staved off financial failure and maintained its independence.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's was given university status on 17 May 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1883, Women's Medical College was founded at Queen's with a class of three.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Theological Hall, completed in 1880, originally served as Queen's main building throughout the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aerial photo of Queen's University, 1919" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg/230px-Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg" width="230" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg/345px-Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg/460px-Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27s_University_from_the_air_1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Queen's University from the air 1919
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1912, Queen's separated from the Presbyterian Church of Scotland and changed its name to Queen's University at Kingston.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Theological_College" title="Queen's Theological College">Queen's Theological College</a> remained in the control of the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Canada" title="Presbyterian Church in Canada">Presbyterian Church in Canada</a>, until 1925, when it joined the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a>, where it remains today.<sup id="cite_ref-theo_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theo-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The university faced another financial crisis during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, from a sharp drop in enrolment due to the military enlistment of students, staff, and faculty. A $1,000,000 fundraising drive and the armistice in 1918 saved the university.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 1,500 students participated in the war and 187 died.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Months before Canada joined <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, US President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, came to Queen's to accept an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degree" title="Honorary degree">honorary degree</a> and, in a broadcast heard around the world, voiced the American policy of mutual alliance and friendship with Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> During World War II, 2,917 graduates from Queen's served in the armed forces, suffering 164 fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The Memorial Room in Memorial Hall of the John Deutsch University Centre lists those Queen's students who fell during the world wars.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's grew quickly after the war, propelled by the expanding postwar economy and the demographic boom that peaked in the 1960s. From 1951 to 1961, enrolment increased from just over 2,000 students to more than 3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The university embarked on a building program, constructing five student residences in less than ten years. Following the reorganization of legal education in Ontario in the mid-1950s, Queen's Faculty of Law opened in 1957 in the newly built John A. Macdonald Hall. Other construction projects at Queen's in the 1950s included the construction of Richardson Hall to house Queen's administrative offices, and Dunning Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the 1960s, like many other universities in Canada, Queen's tripled its enrolment and greatly expanded its faculty, staff, and facilities, as a result of the baby boom and generous support from the public sector. By the mid-1970s, the number of full-time students had reached 10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the new facilities were three more residences and separate buildings for the Departments of Mathematics, Physics, Biology and Psychology, Social Sciences and the Humanities.</p> 
     <p>The period also saw the establishment at Queen's of Schools of Music, Public Administration (now part of Policy Studies), Rehabilitation Therapy, and Urban and Regional Planning. The establishment of the Faculty of Education in 1968 on land about a kilometre west of the university inaugurated the university's west campus.<sup id="cite_ref-hist_2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hist-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:FDRatQueens.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Franklin D. Roosevelt speaking at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/42/FDRatQueens.jpg" width="150" height="166" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:FDRatQueens.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> US President 
        <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a> speaking at Queen's after receiving his honourary degree
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's celebrated its <a href="/wiki/Sesquicentennial" title="Sesquicentennial" class="mw-redirect">sesquicentennial</a> anniversary in 1991, and received a visit from <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Charles, Prince of Wales</a>, and his then-wife, <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana</a>, to mark the occasion. The Prince of Wales presented a replica of the 1841 Royal Charter granted by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, which had established the university; the replica is displayed in the <a href="/wiki/John_Deutsch" title="John Deutsch" class="mw-redirect">John Deutsch</a> University Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The first woman chancellor of Queen's University, Agnes Richardson Benidickson, was installed on 23 October 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-pound2005_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pound2005-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1993, Queen's received Herstmonceux Castle as a donation from alumnus <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Bader" title="Alfred Bader">Alfred Bader</a>. The castle is presently used by the university as the Bader International Study Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-bader_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bader-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twenty-first_century">Twenty-first century</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Twenty-first century">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2001 the Senate Educational Equity Committee (SEEC) studied the experiences of <a href="/wiki/Visible_minority" title="Visible minority">visible minority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_of_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples of Canada" class="mw-redirect">Aboriginal</a> faculty members at Queen's after a black female professor left, alleging that she had experienced racism.<sup id="cite_ref-confront_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confront-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Following this survey SEEC commissioned a study which found that many perceived a 'Culture of Whiteness' at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The report concluded that ?white privilege and power continues to be reflected in the <a href="/wiki/Eurocentric" title="Eurocentric" class="mw-redirect">Eurocentric</a> curricula, traditional pedagogical approaches, hiring, promotion and <a href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure" class="mw-redirect">tenure</a> practices, and opportunities for research? at Queen?s.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's response to the report is the subject of continuing debate.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The administration implemented measures to promote diversity beginning in 2006, such as the position of diversity advisor and the hiring of &quot;dialogue monitors&quot; to facilitate discussions on <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-confront_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-confront-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In May 2010, Queen's University joined the <a href="/wiki/Matariki_Network_of_Universities" title="Matariki Network of Universities">Matariki Network of Universities</a>, an international group of universities created in 2010, which focuses on strong links between research and undergraduate teaching.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Granthall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Grant Hall at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Granthall.JPG/230px-Granthall.JPG" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Granthall.JPG/345px-Granthall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Granthall.JPG/460px-Granthall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Granthall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Grant Hall has been considered the university's most recognized landmark since its completion in 1905.
        <sup id="cite_ref-grant_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grant-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university grounds lies within the neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s,_Kingston" title="Queen's, Kingston">Queen's</a> in the city of Kingston, Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's main campus is bordered to the south by <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_General_Hospital" title="Kingston General Hospital">Kingston General Hospital</a> to the southeast, city parks to the east, and by residential neighbourhoods, known as the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_student_ghetto" title="Kingston student ghetto">Kingston student ghetto</a> or the university district, in all other directions. The campus grew to its present size of 40&nbsp;ha (99&nbsp;acres) through gradual acquisitions of adjacent private lands, and remains the university's largest landholding. The campus's original site and holds the majority of its facilities. In addition to its main campus in Kingston, Queen's owns several other properties around Kingston, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Hinchinbrooke,_Quebec" title="Hinchinbrooke, Quebec">Hinchinbrooke</a>, Quebec, <a href="/wiki/Rideau_Lakes,_Ontario" title="Rideau Lakes, Ontario">Rideau Lakes</a>, Ontario, and East Sussex, England.<sup id="cite_ref-land_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-land-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The buildings at Queen's vary in age, from Summerhill which opened in 1839, to the new <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_School_of_Medicine" title="Queen's School of Medicine">Queen's School of Medicine</a> building, which opened in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Grant Hall, completed in 1905, is considered the university's most recognizable landmark. It is named after Rev. George Munro Grant who served as Queen's seventh principal. The building is used to host concerts, lectures, meetings, exams, and convocations.<sup id="cite_ref-grant_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grant-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Two buildings owned and managed by the university have been listed as <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada" title="National Historic Sites of Canada">National Historic Sites of Canada</a>. The Kingston General Hospital is the oldest operating public hospital in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The Roselawn House, which is located east of the west campus, is the core component of the university's Donald Gordon Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries.2C_museums_and_galleries">Libraries, museums and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Libraries, museums and galleries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stauffer_Library_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Joseph S. Stauffer Library at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Stauffer_Library_2.JPG/230px-Stauffer_Library_2.JPG" width="230" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Stauffer_Library_2.JPG/345px-Stauffer_Library_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Stauffer_Library_2.JPG/460px-Stauffer_Library_2.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stauffer_Library_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Joseph_S._Stauffer_Library" title="Joseph S. Stauffer Library">Joseph S. Stauffer Library</a> is the largest library at the university, and holds the main collection for humanities and social science.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's University Libraries include six campus libraries in five facilities housing 2.2 million physical items and 400,000 electronic resources, including e-books, serial titles and databases. The library's budget in 2007?2008 was $18.1 million, with $9.8 million dedicated to acquisitions.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The libraries are <a href="/wiki/Bracken_Health_Sciences_Library" title="Bracken Health Sciences Library">Bracken Health Sciences Library</a>, Education Library,<sup id="cite_ref-libs_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libs-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Lederman Law Library, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_S._Stauffer_Library" title="Joseph S. Stauffer Library">Stauffer Humanities and Social Sciences Library</a> and Engineering &amp; Science Library. The W.D. Jordan Special Collections and Music Library notably harbors early-dated books from 1475?1700.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The Engineering &amp; Science Library and the W.D. Jordan Library Special Collections and Music Library share facilities, known as Douglas Library.<sup id="cite_ref-libs_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libs-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's operates the Miller Museum of Geology, an earth-science teaching museum which features an Earth Science and Geological Collections of 10 000 Minerals, and 865 fossils as well as an exhibit of the geology of the Kingston area. The museum is largely used as an earth-science teaching museum for local schools and natural-science interest groups in eastern Ontario.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The permanent exhibits feature dinosaurs, dinosaur eggs, fossils of early multi-celled animals and land tracks fossilized from 500 million years ago. <sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's art collections are housed at the <a href="/wiki/Agnes_Etherington_Art_Centre" title="Agnes Etherington Art Centre">Agnes Etherington Art Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The art centre owes its namesake to Agnes Etherington, whose house was donated to the university and is being used as an art museum.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Opened in 1957, it contains over 14,000 works of art, including works by <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inuit_art" title="Inuit art">Inuit art</a>. The Union Gallery, an art gallery opened in 1994, is run by the university's student body and faculty. The gallery is dedicated to the promotion of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_and_student_facilities">Housing and student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Housing and student facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university has sixteen student residences: Adelaide Hall, Ban Righ Hall, Chown Hall, Gordon House, Brockington House, Graduate Residence, Harkness Hall, John Orr Tower Apartments, Leggett Hall, Leonard Hall, McNeill House, Morris Hall, Victoria Hall, Waldron Tower, Watts Hall and Jean Royce Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest is Victoria Hall, built in 1965, which houses nearly 900 students.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2010, 83.3 percent of first-year students lived on campus, part of the 26 percent of the overall undergraduate population which lived on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Residents are represented by two groups, the Main Campus Residents' Council, which represents the main campus, and the Jean Royce Hall Council, which represents the west campus (Jean Royce Hall, Harkness International Hall and the Graduate Residence). They are responsible for representing resident concerns, providing entertainment services, organizing events and upholding rules and regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Life Centre is the centre of student governance and student directed social, cultural, entertainment and recreational activities. The Student Life Centre consists of the John Deutsch University Centre (JDUC), Grey House, Carruthers Hall, Queen?s Journal House, MacGillivray-Brown Hall, and the non-athletic sections of Queen's Centre. Collectively, these buildings provide 10,500 square metres (113,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) of space to the Queen's community.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The JDUC contains the offices of a number of student organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_Society_of_Queen%27s_University" title="Alma Mater Society of Queen's University">Alma Mater Society of Queen's University</a>, as well as retail and food services.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has sixteen food outlets located throughout the campus, as well as three major residence dining facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Off_campus_facilities">Off campus facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Off campus facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG/230px-Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG/345px-Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG/460px-Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Herstmonceux_Castle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Herstmonceux Castle, which houses the Bader International Study Centre
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's has a number of off-campus faculties located throughout Kingston and abroad. The university has a second campus located in Kingston, known as the west campus. The west campus, acquired in 1969, is 2&nbsp;km (1.2&nbsp;mi) west of the main campus, and covers 27&nbsp;ha (67&nbsp;acres) of land. The west campus has two student residences, the Faculty of Education, the Coastal Engineering Lab, and several athletic facilities, including the <a href="/wiki/Richardson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Richardson Memorial Stadium">Richardson Memorial Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2007, the university had approved the designs for the Isabel Bader Centre for Performing Arts, also located in Kingston. The new centre for performing arts is expected to open in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university owns a research facility in Rideau Lakes, Ontario, known as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University_Biological_Station" title="Queen's University Biological Station">Queen's University Biological Station</a>. Opened during the 1950s, the field station encompasses approximately 3000 hectares of property, a range of habitat types typical of Eastern Ontario, and many species of conservation concern in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen?s has an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Novelis_Inc." title="Novelis Inc." class="mw-redirect">Novelis Inc.</a> to acquire a 20-hectare (49-acre) property adjacent to the company's research and development centre in Kingston.<sup id="cite_ref-queensu1_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queensu1-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The agreement is part of the plan to establish an innovative technology park located at the corner of Princess and Concession streets, which is to be called Innovation Park at Queen's University. The property was acquired for $5.3 million, a portion of the $21 million grant Queen's received from the Ontario government last spring to pioneer this innovative new regional R&amp;D &quot;co-location&quot; model.<sup id="cite_ref-queensu1_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queensu1-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's leases approximately 7,900 square metres (85,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) of the Novelis R&amp;D facilities to accommodate both faculty-led research projects that have industrial partners and small and medium-size companies with a research focus and a desire to interact with Queen's researchers. The remainder of the government funds support further development of the technology park to transform the property into a welcoming and dynamic site for business expansion and relocation.<sup id="cite_ref-queensu1_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queensu1-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Bader International Study Centre (BISC) is housed in <a href="/wiki/Herstmonceux_Castle" title="Herstmonceux Castle">Herstmonceux Castle</a>, East Sussex, England, which was donated to Queen's in 1993 by alumnus <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Bader" title="Alfred Bader">Alfred Bader</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bader_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bader-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> BISC is academically fully integrated with Queen's, although financially self-sufficient. Its mission is to provide academic programs for undergraduate students whose academic interests are oriented toward the United Kingdom, Europe and the European Union, continuing-education programs for executives and other professional or ?special interest? groups, a venue for conferences and meetings, a base for international graduate students and other scholars undertaking research in the United Kingdom and Europe and as an enhanced educational, social and cultural environment for the local community, using the unique heritage of the castle.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The opportunity to study at the BISC is not limited to Queen's students. Queen's has academic exchange agreements with universities in Canada and internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Queen's Sustainability Office, which was created in 2008, is charged with the university's green initiatives and creating awareness about environmental issues.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The office is headed by a Sustainability Manager, who works with the university, external community groups and the government. In 2009, with the signing of the agreement, the <i>Ontario Universities Committed to a Greener World</i>, Queen's had pledged to transform its campus into a model of environmental responsibility.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's was the second Ontario university to sign the <i>University and College Presidents? Climate Change Statement of Action for Canada</i>, in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university campus received a B grade from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Academics at Queen's is organized into ten undergraduate, graduate and professional faculties and schools.<sup id="cite_ref-ugpfs_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ugpfs-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The governance of the university is conducted through the Board of Trustees, the Senate, and the University Council, all three of which were established under the Royal Charter of 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-roycha_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roycha-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board is responsible for the university's conduct and management and its property, revenues, business, and affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-qbot_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qbot-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Ex officio governors of the Board include the university's chancellor, principal and the rector. The Board has 34 other trustees, 33 of which are elected by the various members of the university community, including elected representatives from the student body. The representative from Queen's Theological College is the only appointed trustee.<sup id="cite_ref-qbot_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qbot-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Senate is responsible for determining all academic matters affecting the university as a whole, including student discipline.<sup id="cite_ref-qsen_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsen-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate consists of 17 ex officio positions granted to the principal and vice-chancellor, the vice-principals of the university, the senior dean of each faculty, dean of student affairs, the deputy provost, and the presidents of the undergraduate, graduate and faculty associations. The Senate also consists of 55 other members, appointed or elected by various communities of the university including elected representatives of the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-qsen_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsen-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Queensquad.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Gordon Hall at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Queensquad.JPG/200px-Queensquad.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Queensquad.JPG/300px-Queensquad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Queensquad.JPG/400px-Queensquad.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Queensquad.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Gordon Hall houses many of Queen's administrative offices.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Royal Charter of 1841 was amended to include the University Council in 1874. The Council is a composite of the Board of Trustees, senators and an equal number of elected graduates. It serves as both an advisory and an ambassadorial body to the university as a whole and is responsible for the election of the chancellor.<sup id="cite_ref-quc_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quc-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Although it is not directly involved in operations, the Council may bring to the Senate or Board of Trustees any matter that it believes affects Queen's well-being. The Council meets once per year, typically in May.<sup id="cite_ref-quc_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quc-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i>Chancellor</i> is the highest officer and the ceremonial head of the university. The office was created in 1874 and first filled in 1877, although it was only enshrined in law in 1882 after its amendment into the Royal Charter of 1841. The responsibilities of the chancellor includes presiding over convocations, conferring degrees, chairing the annual meetings of the Council and is an ex officio, voting member of the Board of Trustees. A person is elected to the office of chancellor on a three-year term by the Council unless there is more than one candidate, in which case an election is conducted among Queen's graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i>Principal</i> acts as the <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> of the university under the authority of the Board and the Senate, and supervises and directs the academic and administrative work of the university and of its teaching and non-teaching staff.<sup id="cite_ref-roycha_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roycha-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 1974, principals were appointed for five-year terms, renewable subject to review. The formal authority for the appointment of the Principal rests under the Royal Charter with the Board of Trustees although recent principals have been selected by a joint committee of trustees and senators.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2013 <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Woolf" title="Daniel Woolf">Daniel Woolf</a> was the twentieth principal, serving since 1 September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The office of the vice-chancellor has typically been held by the incumbent principal. In 1961, an amendment was secured by the Board to separate the office of principal from vice-chancellor if it wished. The first, and only person to ever hold the office of vice-chancellor, but not the office of principal, was <a href="/wiki/William_Archibald_Mackintosh" title="William Archibald Mackintosh">William Archibald Mackintosh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university completed the 2011-2012 year with revenues of $769.9 million and expenses of $773.3 million, yielding a deficit of $3.4 million. Government grants made up 48 percent of the 2011?12 operating budget. Student fees made up 28 percent of the 2010?11 operating budget.<sup id="cite_ref-qrotab_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrotab-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 30 April 2012, Queen's endowment was valued at C$584.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-qrotab_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrotab-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has been registered as an educational charitable organization by <a href="/wiki/Canada_Revenue_Agency" title="Canada Revenue Agency">Canada Revenue Agency</a> since 1 January 1967. As of 2011, the university registered primarily as a post-secondary institution, with 70 percent of the charity dedicated to management and maintenance. The charity has 21 percent dedicated towards research, while the remaining 8 percent has been dedicated towards awards, bursaries and scholarships. Proceeds from the charity also go toward Queen's Theological College (as an affiliated college) and the Bader International Study Centre at Herstmonceaux Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Queen's is a publicly funded research university, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The full-time undergraduate programs comprise the majority of the school's enrolment, made up of 14,951 full-time undergraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-Quick_Facts_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quick_Facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009 the two largest programs by enrolment were the social sciences, with 3,286 full-time and part-time students, followed by engineering, with 3,097 full-time and part-time students.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The university conferred 3,232 bachelor degrees, 153 doctoral degrees, 1,142 master degrees, and 721 first professional degrees in 2008?2009.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="infobox" cellspacing="3" style="border-spacing:3px;width:22em;width:23em; font-size:75%;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;"><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">University rankings</a></th> 
       </tr>

       </tr>

        <td>201?300</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="College and university rankings">ARWU</a></i> Life Sciences<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></th>

       </tr>

        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i> World<sup id="cite_ref-QS_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>175</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">THE-WUR</a></i> World<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></th>

        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="College and university rankings">ARWU</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>8-17</td>

       <tr> 
        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s#University_Ranking_Guide" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> Medical/Doctoral<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>4</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">THE-WUR</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></th>
