       <tr> 
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:right;"> 
         <div class="noprint plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style=""> 
          <ul> 
           <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template:Canadian university rankings"><span title="View this template" style="">v</span></a></li> 
           <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template talk:Canadian university rankings"><span title="Discuss this template" style="">t</span></a></li> 
           <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Canadian_university_rankings&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style="">e</span></a></li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Queen's University has consistently been ranked one of Canada's top universities. The 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the university 175th in the world, and the seventh in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) rankings, the university ranked 201?300th in the world and ranked 8-17 in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same year, ARWU had also ranked the Queen's 101-150th in the field of social sciences, and 151-200th in the field of life and agricultural sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012?2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> placed Queen's 201-225th in the world, and ninth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of national rankings, <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> ranked Queen's 4th in their 2011 Medical Doctoral university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup>Queen's University Faculty of Law was ranked third nationally in Maclean's 2012 rankings for <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> schools in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> In the field of geography, Queen's was ranked 41st in the world, and fourth in the country by the 2013 QS World University Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's School of Business's has received significant recognition in the past years. The School of Business placed 48th in the world, in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Business_Insiders" title="Business Insiders">Business Insiders</a> business school rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a>'s 2012 ranking of business schools, the School of Business was rated as a 5 palmes business school, placing the school 37th globally, and fourth nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 edition of <a href="/wiki/Mines_ParisTech" title="Mines ParisTech">Mines ParisTech's</a> evaluation of universities, The School of Business was also found to have the most number graduates employed as Chief Executive Officers (or equivalent) in a <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a>, out of any university in Canada, and 38th globally.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In an employability survey published by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> in October 2011, when CEOs and chairpersons were asked to select the top universities which they recruited from, the university placed 74th in the world, and fifth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The full-time MBA program at Queen's has also received significant recognition. The school was ranked first in Canada, and fourth in the world outside of the United States by <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a>'s 2012 ranking of MBA programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The QS ranking of North American MBA programs placed the School of Business 16th in North America, and 3rd in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a> rankings on <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration#Basic_types_of_MBA_programs" title="Master of Business Administration">EMBA</a> programs, Queen's joint degree business programs with <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Curtis_Johnson_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management">Samuel Curtis Johnson Graduate School of Management</a> was ranked 45th in the world. In the same rankings, the Financial Times ranked the Queen's School of Business's individual EMBA program 92nd in the world, and fourth in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sudbury_sno.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The neutrino detector at the Sudbury Neutrino Observatory" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Sudbury_sno.jpg/200px-Sudbury_sno.jpg" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Sudbury_sno.jpg/300px-Sudbury_sno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Sudbury_sno.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sudbury_sno.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Queen's physicists are among those involved in research conducted at the Sudbury Neutrino Observatory.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In Research Infosource's 2011 ranking of Canada's 50 top research universities, Queen's ranked 11th, with sponsored research income of $197.016 million. With an average of $237,900 per faculty member, Queen's ranked Canada's sixth most research-intensive university.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> The federal government is the largest funding source, providing 49.8 percent of Queen's research budget, primarily through grants. Corporations contribute another 26.3 percent of the research budget.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of research performance, <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> 2010 ranked Queen's 185th out of 500 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT), an organization which evaluates universities based on the <a href="/wiki/Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">performance of scientific papers</a>, ranked Queen's 272nd.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university operates six research centres and institutes, the Centre for Neuroscience Studies, GeoEngeering Centre, High Performance Computing Virtual Laboratory, Human Mobility Research Centre, <a href="/wiki/Sudbury_Neutrino_Observatory" title="Sudbury Neutrino Observatory">Sudbury Neutrino Observatory Institute</a>, and the Southern African Research Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sudbury Neutrino Observatory's director, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_B._McDonald" title="Arthur B. McDonald">Arthur B. McDonald</a>, is a member of the university's physics department. The observatory managed the SNO experiment, which demonstrated that the solution to the <a href="/wiki/Solar_neutrino_problem" title="Solar neutrino problem">solar neutrino problem</a> was that neutrinos change flavour (type) as they propagate through the Sun. The SNO experiment proved that a non-zero mass neutrino exists. This was a major breakthrough in cosmology.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's University has a joint venture with McGill University, operating an academic publishing house known as the <a href="/wiki/McGill-Queen%27s_University_Press" title="McGill-Queen's University Press">McGill-Queen's University Press</a>. It publishes original peer-reviewed and books in all areas of the social sciences and humanities. While the press's emphasis is on providing an outlet for Canadian authors and scholarship, the press also publishes authors throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The press has over 2,800 books in print.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The publishing house was known as the McGill University Press in 1963 prior to it amalgamating with Queen's in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admission">Admission</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Admission">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The requirements for admission differ between students from Ontario, other provinces in Canada, and international students due to the lack of uniformity in marking schemes. The acceptance rate at Queen's for full-time, first-year applications in 2012 was 41 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the secondary school average for full-time first-year students at Queen's was 88.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> The application process emphasizes the mandatory Personal Statement of Experience (PSE). The statement expresses how the applicant's personal experiences may contribute to the university. It focuses on qualifications and involvement outside of academics and is an important factor in determining admission. Several faculties require applicants to submit a supplementary essay.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Students may apply for financial aid such as the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Student_Assistance_Program" title="Ontario Student Assistance Program">Ontario Student Assistance Program</a> and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans and Grants</a> through the federal and provincial governments. The financial aid provided may come in the form of loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2010?11 academic year, Queen's provided $36.5 million worth of student financial assistance in the form of both need-based and merit-based assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-qrotab_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrotab-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG/220px-Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG/330px-Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Frosh_Week_at_Queens.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Frosh Week festivities at Queen's University
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The student body of Queen's is represented by two <a href="/wiki/Students%27_unions" title="Students' unions" class="mw-redirect">students' unions</a>, the Alma Mater Society (AMS) for all undergraduate students and the Society of Graduate and Professional Students for graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-alma_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alma-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> The AMS of Queen's University is the oldest undergraduate student government in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-alma_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alma-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The AMS recognizes more than 170 student clubs and organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> All accredited extracurricular organizations at Queen's fall under the jurisdiction of either the AMS, or the Society of Graduate and Professional Students.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The organizations and clubs accredited at Queen's cover a wide range of interests including academics, culture, religion, social issues, and recreation. The oldest accredited club at Queen's is the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Debating_Union" title="Queen's Debating Union">Queen's Debating Union</a>, which was formed in 1843 and originally named the Dialectic Society.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The Dialectic Society had also served as a form of student government, until the AMS was formed from the dialectic society in 1858.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Bands" title="Queen's Bands">Queen's Bands</a> is a student marching band founded in 1905, which claims to be the largest and oldest student marching band in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Fraternities and sororities have been banned at the university, since a ruling made by the AMS in 1933. The ruling was passed in response to the formation of two fraternities in the 1920s. No accredited sororities have ever existed at Queen's.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The AMS also manages the Student Constable peer to peer security service at the university. They are responsible for ensuring the safety of patrons and staff at sanctioned events and venues across the campus, enforce governing regulations of the AMS and uphold regulations stipulated in the <a href="/wiki/Liquor_Licence_Act_(Ontario)" title="Liquor Licence Act (Ontario)">Liquor Licence Act of Ontario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> In spite of their mandate however, Student Constables do not serve as the university's primary security service as they are legally not <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_officer" title="Law enforcement officer" class="mw-redirect">peace officers</a>, nor are they registered as a private security service under the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Community_Safety_and_Correctional_Services" title="Ministry of Community Safety and Correctional Services">Ministry of Community Safety and Correctional Services</a>. The university's administration operates its own security service which is registered in Ontario as a private security service.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> As of March 2012, the Student Constables are funded through a mandatory $10 fee levied on undergraduates annually by the AMS.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Queen's University's student population operates a number of media outlets throughout the campus environment. <a href="/wiki/The_Queen%27s_Journal" title="The Queen's Journal">The Queen's Journal</a> is Queen's main <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a>. During the academic year, the Queen's Journal publishes two issues a week, until the last month of the semester, when only one issue is published each week. In total the Queen's Journal publishes 40 issues a year. The newspaper was established in 1873, making it one of the oldest student newspapers in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The other weekly student publication from Queen's is the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Words" title="Golden Words">Golden Words</a>, a weekly humour publication managed by the Engineering Society.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's student population also runs a radio station, <a href="/wiki/CFRC" title="CFRC" class="mw-redirect">CFRC</a>. Queen's radio station is the longest running campus-based broadcaster in the world, and the second longest running radio station in the world, surpassed only by the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_plc" title="Marconi plc" class="mw-redirect">Marconi companies</a>. The first public broadcast of the station was on 27 October 1923 when the football game between Queen's and McGill was called play-by-play. Since 2001, the station has broadcast on a 24-hour schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1980, the university also has a student-run television service, known as <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_TV" title="Queen's TV">Queen's TV</a>. The television station airs every weekday on its website, and every Wednesday on local television.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27sRichardson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Richardson Memorial Stadium at Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Queen%27sRichardson.jpg/220px-Queen%27sRichardson.jpg" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Queen%27sRichardson.jpg/330px-Queen%27sRichardson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Queen%27sRichardson.jpg/440px-Queen%27sRichardson.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Queen%27sRichardson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Richardson Memorial Stadium is the home to Queen's varsity football team.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Golden_Gaels" title="Queen's Golden Gaels">Queen's Golden Gaels</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Sport teams at Queen's University are known as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Golden_Gaels" title="Queen's Golden Gaels">Golden Gaels</a>. The Golden Gaels sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference for most varsity sports. Varsity teams at Queen's include basketball, cross country, Canadian football, ice hockey, rowing, rugby, soccer and volleyball. The athletics program at Queen's University dates back to 1873. With 39 regional and national championships, Queen's football program has secured more championships than any other sport team at Queen's, and more than any other football team in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Gael_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gael-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> are the only universities to have claimed <a href="/wiki/Grey_Cup" title="Grey Cup">Grey Cups</a> (1922, 1923 and 1924), now the championship trophy for the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a>. Queen?s also competed for the <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> in 1894?95, 1898?99 and 1905?06.<sup id="cite_ref-Gael_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gael-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Queen's University has a number of athletic facilities open to both their varsity teams as well as to their students. The stadium with the largest seating capacity at Queen's is <a href="/wiki/Richardson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Richardson Memorial Stadium">Richardson Memorial Stadium</a>. Built in 1971, the stadium seats over 10,000 and is home to the varsity football team.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The stadium has also played host for a number of international games including Canada's second round <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_CONCACAF_Second_Round" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification ? CONCACAF Second Round">2006 FIFA World Cup qualification games</a> and the inaugural match for the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Cup_(rugby_league)" title="Colonial Cup (rugby league)">Colonial Cup</a>, an international rugby league challenge match.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Other athletic facilities at Queen's include the Athletic and Recreation Centre, which houses a number of gymnasiums and pools; Tindall Field, a multi-season playing field and jogging track; Kingston Field, home to the school's rugby teams; and West Campus Fields, which is used by a number of varsity teams and student intramural leagues.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Insignias_and_other_representations">Insignias and other representations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Insignias and other representations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_Arms">Coat of Arms</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coat of Arms">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> appeared as early as 1850, but was not registered with the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Arms" title="College of Arms">College of Arms</a> until 1953. The coat of arms was registered with the Scottish equivalent of the College of Arms, the <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">Lord Lyon King of Arms</a>, in 1981 and with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Heraldic_Authority" title="Canadian Heraldic Authority">Canadian Heraldic Authority</a> during Queen's sesquicentennial celebrations in 1991. The coat of arms is based off the University of Edinburgh, the institution after which Queen's was modelled.<sup id="cite_ref-arms_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arms-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Coat of Arms consists of a gold shield with red edges, divided into four triangular compartments by a blue, diagonal <a href="/wiki/Saltire" title="Saltire">St. Andrew's Cross</a>. A golden book, symbolizing learning, sits open at the centre of the cross. In each of the four compartments is an emblem of the university's Canadian and British origins: a pine tree for Canada, a thistle for Scotland, a rose for England, and a shamrock for Ireland. The border is decorated with eight gold crowns, symbolic of Queen Victoria and the university's Royal Charter.<sup id="cite_ref-arms_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arms-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto_and_song">Motto and song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Motto and song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Queen's motto, chosen from <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Isaiah</a> 33:6 is <i>Sapientia et Doctrina Stabilitas</i>. The Latin motto is literally translated as &quot;Wisdom and knowledge shall be the stability of thy times,&quot; and has been in use since the 1850s.<sup id="cite_ref-mottos_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mottos-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> A number of songs are commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic contests, including the &quot;Queen's College Colours&quot; (1897) also known as &quot;Our University Yell&quot; and &quot;<a href="/wiki/Oil_Thigh" title="Oil Thigh">Oil Thigh</a>&quot;, with words by A.E. Lavell, sung to the tune '<a href="/wiki/John_Brown%27s_Body" title="John Brown's Body">John Brown's Body</a>'.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Oil Thigh, which was created in 1891, consists of the old song &quot;Queen's College Colours&quot;. The name &quot;Oil Thigh&quot; comes from the chorus of the song, which begins with the <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Gaelic</a> words oil thigh. The modern version of the song was crafted in 1985, when a line was changed to include Queen's woman athletes in the cheer.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Queens_University_(Canada).svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Queen's University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg/200px-Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg.png" width="200" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg/300px-Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg/400px-Flag_of_Queens_University_%28Canada%29.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Queens_University_(Canada).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Blue, gold and red are the official colours of the university, and can be seen on its flag.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's official colours are gold, blue, and red.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's colours are also used on the school flag. It displays three vertical stripes one for each colour. In the upper left corner on the blue stripe is a crown in yellow symbolizing the royal charter.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also has a ceremonial flag, which is reserved for official university uses. The ceremonial flag is a square design of the Queen's coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university also has a <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">tartan</a> made up of six colours, each representing an academic discipline: blue (medicine), red (arts &amp; science), gold (applied science), white (nursing science), green (commerce &amp; MBA), and Purple (theology). The tartan was created in 1966 by Judge John Matheson and is registered under the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Tartans_Authority" title="Scottish Tartans Authority">Scottish Tartans Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen%27s_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:David_A._Dodge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photo of David A. Dodge" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/David_A._Dodge.jpg/150px-David_A._Dodge.jpg" width="150" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/David_A._Dodge.jpg/225px-David_A._Dodge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/David_A._Dodge.jpg/300px-David_A._Dodge.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:David_A._Dodge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/David_A._Dodge" title="David A. Dodge">David A. Dodge</a>, former Governor of the Bank of Canada, graduate of Queen's and its current Chancellor.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Queen%27s_University_people" title="List of Queen's University people">List of Queen's University people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Queen's graduates have found success in a variety of fields, heading diverse institutions in the public and private sectors. I In 2011, there were over 131,000 alumni, living in 156 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-alum1_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alum1-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen's faculty and graduates have won many awards including the <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JFOOTE_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFOOTE-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2009, 56 Queen's students and graduates had been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhode_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhode-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable politicians who were once Chancellor include <a href="/wiki/Robert_Borden" title="Robert Borden">Robert Borden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roland_Michener" title="Roland Michener">Roland Michener</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, and provincial premiers <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lougheed" title="Peter Lougheed">Peter Lougheed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Avery_Dunning" title="Charles Avery Dunning">Charles Avery Dunning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson198346_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson198346-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson1983226_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson1983226-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Many alumni have gained international prominence for serving in government, such as <a href="/wiki/Norihito,_Prince_Takamado" title="Norihito, Prince Takamado" class="mw-redirect">Prince Takamado</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_House_of_Japan" title="Imperial House of Japan">Imperial House of Japan</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_O._Hall" title="Kenneth O. Hall">Kenneth O. Hall</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Jamaica" title="Governor General of Jamaica" class="mw-redirect">Governor General of Jamaica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> The 28th <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Johnston" title="David Johnston">David Johnston</a>, was a former graduate and faculty member of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Three Canadian premiers graduated from Queen's, <a href="/wiki/William_Aberhart" title="William Aberhart">William Aberhart</a>, the 7th <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Alberta" title="Premier of Alberta">Premier of Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_McKenna" title="Frank McKenna">Frank McKenna</a>, the 27th <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_New_Brunswick" title="Premier of New Brunswick">Premier of New Brunswick</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Wynne" title="Kathleen Wynne">Kathleen Wynne</a>, the 25th <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">Premier of Ontario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The 14th Premier of Alberta, <a href="/wiki/Alison_Redford" title="Alison Redford">Alison Redford</a> studied at the university for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cromwell" title="Thomas Cromwell">Thomas Cromwell</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Justices_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="List of Justices of the Supreme Court of Canada">Justice</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a> was also a graduate from the university.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Business leaders who studied at Queen's include <a href="/wiki/Derek_Burney" title="Derek Burney">Derek Burney</a>, former chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Bell_Canada" title="Bell Canada">Bell Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Donald_J._Carty" title="Donald J. Carty">Donald J. Carty</a>, chairman of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_America" title="Virgin America">Virgin America</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porter_Airlines" title="Porter Airlines">Porter Airlines</a> and former chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/AMR_Corporation" title="AMR Corporation">AMR Corporation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Earle_McLaughlin" title="Earle McLaughlin">Earle McLaughlin</a>, former president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Canada" title="Royal Bank of Canada">Royal Bank of Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Nixon" title="Gordon Nixon">Gordon Nixon</a>, president and CEO of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Canada" title="Royal Bank of Canada">Royal Bank of Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kimbal_Musk" title="Kimbal Musk">Kimbal Musk</a>, founders of <a href="/wiki/OneRiot" title="OneRiot">OneRiot</a>, <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_A._Dodge" title="David A. Dodge">David A. Dodge</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_the_Bank_of_Canada" title="Governor of the Bank of Canada">Governor of the Bank of Canada</a> and the university's current chancellor is similarly a Queen's graduate.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sandford_Fleming" title="Sandford Fleming">Sandford Fleming</a>, an engineer and inventor who was known for proposing worldwide standard <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a> also served as the Chancellor of Queen's.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
